<Rating>5< /Rating>< text>
Very good food. I ordered a tri tip combo plate for 15.95.  The tri tip was cooked with onion and it came with bread, rice, black beans, salad and some grind pork skin.  Everything was nicely flavored and not salty.  The place is a little shack with cute outdoor seating (about 20 seats maybe? ). And the owner (I assume) really loves dogs.  So bring your furry friends.  Btw, they have an additional location only a few blocks away that is in a building if you prefer indoor dining more.<//text>

<Text>Definitely a must try place in Berkeley. I've been coming here for the past ten years and I have yet to find a better tri tip in the Bay Area. The only dishes I ever get are the tri tip sandwich, the tri tip salad, and the tri tip plate. Their tri tip is amazing.

The shack itself has some really fun design to it. It's like a food stand you'd see on a beach, but in reality it's in Downtown Berkeley right next to the main city roads. Definitely the kind of quirky place you'd expect out of Berkeley. I'd highly recommend bringing first time visitors here.

Pedro's an awesome dude and always hands out free samples. You'll probably see him standing outside the stand clapping to the music.<//Text></record></dataset><record>

<review>Ive been away from shooting for a few years. I went to the Beaumont indoor range 7/17 to get back into it. The owner Casey is awesome!! He gave me a refresher on safety and range rules, checked my ammo, and gave me a lane. After a few magazines, he came out to the line, said I was shooting well, and offered some tips on my grip. His advice tightened my grouping!
I was having trouble with one of my pistols that hadnt been fired in a while. It failed to feed a few times. We field stripped it, and Casey jumped in and oiled the rails and barrel really quick. It still had the issue, so he grabbed a mag from the store, had me run some rounds through it, no more failures. My mag springs were weak.
The facility is clean and really well run. Casey was really cool, and helpfull. Ill be back for sure!!< /review><userid>103270198265130382218</userid>< Date>

< review>
You get what you pay for. In a good way. Its a little expensive to shoot here, and you can't pick up your brass.

Those are the only negatives in my book. And neither are deal breakers. I have probably shot here 15 times. It is in a convenient location, clean, well working range, with friendly staff and a focus on safety.

The staff are also decently knowledgeable on gun laws, yeah sure there are probably some holes in their knowledge, we live in California. The land of 10,000 gun laws. But they seem to do a good job at staying current.

From what I've seen, they dont needlessly hassle experienced shooters, and are friendly and helpful with new shooters.

Today I also took their LTC class for riverside county, great experience, good knowledge, and the instructor kept the class interesting, while getting through 8 hours of information.

Basically I would recommend this place, and I do to my friends and family.<//review>

< username>
Joe Biesek<//username>
<Date>1456303961389</Date><rate>3</rate>< Review>
An excellent shooting range for new or "beginner" shooters where tips on weapon safety and handling are offered by the staff. They also offer a discount to first responders (i.e. LE, Fire, EMS) on lane fees which is a very nice gesture.

However...don't think twice about picking up your brass (not allowed) and if you bring an AR and the owner is on premises be prepared for an inspection mid-shoot while you're in your lane. He'll play it off like he's really interested in your AR but all he's doing is making sure that your AR is properly neutered, I mean, CA complaint (read: bullet button equipped). This kind of scrutiny is just short of a rubber glove prostate exam and it'll make you rethink about heading to an outdoor range.</Review>

< Review>
I've been coming here at least once a month for a year or so now.
First time I walked in I felt like I loved the place. It feels spacious, it's well lit and has upbeat music playing.
Most products are displayed out on the floor area so I can walk around and browse before getting in line. They compensate for heavy taxes with several different discount types so you can pay a reasonable price for everything.
Lastly, I'm a type of customer who usually picks a favorite employee that I kinda latch on to. I haven't been able to here. I think I have the same positive vibes from everyone there.
I have yet to have an experience I'd qualify as negative in any way.</Review>

4‚≠êÔ∏è The types of meat (Only have üêì, ü¶ê, üêÑ, & fishball, NO pork?! What the heck?);
4‚≠êÔ∏è The price (The entrees are between $9-$13; the drinks are expensive $4 to begin with; deserts? Do they even have desert!? Lol);
3‚≠êÔ∏è The knowledge of what the bistro sells of the cashier/person who placed the order for me.
3‚≠êÔ∏è The portion of the dish;
3‚≠êÔ∏è The presentation of the dish;

3.6‚≠êÔ∏è

To be honest, I didn‚Äôt expect that I would have find such authentic Hong Kong style curry rice in this neighborhood, I am totally amazed & surprised!

The menu is a bare bone, but it‚Äôs definitely a lot of room for growth, so does the kitchen, since they have the kitchen already, why don‚Äôt they just fully utilized the resource they have to provide more varieties of dishes.

This is the 2nd time I went back to this Bistro, because of its taste of food totally reminded me of what Hong Kong style comfort food tastes like, and the portion from last time was decent, however this time the portion was significantly smaller than last time, so this is an opportunity to work on delivering/regulating their portions.

And I know it might seem to look a little bit harsh to even put the presentation of the dish as part of the rating, however, food is not just food, by the end of the day food is also piece of art no matter if it comes from a bad neighborhood cheap bistro or a 5 stars Michelin star chef restaurant. If I would rate an upscale restaurant for their presentation of how their dishes like, I should do the same for this too.

Anyway, in a conclusion, this is really not a bad taste food place at all, just need to work on the variety of the menu they provide, regulate the portions of dishes.< /Text>

< Text>
This is a legit sammie shop!  Super tasty.  Next to the El Cajon courthouse, their theme is all legal jargon (kinda funny)!

The menu is smaller than an average deli for sandwich options, but the flavors and the toppings are very well put together.  There is something for everyone no doubt!

<user_name>That One Guy, Remember.<//user_name><time>1594680010939</time>< review>
Christmas circle in Borrego always reminds me of that scene in the Griswold's European vacation.  Stuck in the endless circle & can't get out. Haha!
With that being said, it is a cool spot to have a packed lunch or enjoy a snack you picked up in town, while taking in the scenery.   We normally stop in that area during the winter months. We like to check out the artworks that are around the area. Most can be seen from the roadway but, there are well traveled trails to get up close. Fun way to engage with nature & explore new parts of the desert. Most standard car's can make it. Just go slow & take ur time.  Borrego springs is a beautiful area, help keep it that way. Take out what u bring in.  It takes a tribe.  We always enjoy our visits down there. I'm sure you will too!< /review>

< username>
Erica Peterson<//username>
<resp>None< /resp>< Review>
Every year at the end of October, "Borrego Days" begins. This event has been reoccurring for over 50 yrs. The 3 day event begins on a Friday and lasts through Sunday evening. There is an annual "Miss Borrego Springs" Pageant prior to Fridays kickoff and then on Saturday there is a 9 am Parade. Thru the weekend, there are vendors selling various items such as handmade jewelry, drinks, food, speciality items, toys, a jumper for kids ALL & more at Christmas Circle! I went on Sunday this year and there was a very popular & famous live band from Sinaloa, Mexico. Great Music! Lots of people dancing! Enjoying themselves and sharing with one another! After all, we are a small town of approx. 3500 people. There are many restaurants you can eat at when you come to Borrego. Like Carlees, which has a bar, pool tables, Dinning area, Music & Karioke. There's Pablitos Mexican, Jilbertos Taco Shop, Kendall's Cafe (Which is my favorite place in Borrego, eat in or order by phone for pick up, carry out) El Borrego Mex, Red Ocotillo ( the Hamburgers are SUPERB), Palm Canyon Resort, which just recently changed there menu (and I think it was great and easier to order) and prices very reasonable. They have a Saloon where you can order n eat there as well.. (employees seem intuitive and always smiling) So, put it in your calendar for next year and come on down and enjoy, relax, unwind and share a memorable weekend as a family!!!<//Review>
